(24th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The General Headquarters convened a military expenditure meeting on the afternoon of the 24th, where Chairman Chiang had a detailed discussion on the allocation of military expenses for various armies. According to a senior official of the headquarters, after the amount of military expenditure for each unit is determined, the military department will issue the monthly pay and provisions and send personnel to various places to issue them by name, in order to ensure accuracy and avoid wasting national funds. (24th Dispatch)

Shao Lizi Discusses Zhang Xueliang's Election 31

(Nanjing) There are considerable doubts in society regarding Zhang Xueliang's election as a Central Supervisory Committee member. A reporter interviewed Central Committee member Shao Lizi yesterday, inquiring about his opinion. Shao responded that when the Japanese army suddenly occupied Liaoning and Jilin, Zhang was in Beiping and failed to take precautions in advance, and public opinion is certainly justified in blaming him. However, when evaluating people and events, we should focus on the overall interests of the nation. When the Northern Expedition was about to be completed in the 17th year of the Republic, Zhang resolutely changed the flag, completing the unification of the country, despite various internal and external threats and obstructions. This action greatly angered the Japanese, but it was a contribution to the nation. Later, he joined our party, supported the central government, and consolidated unification. Even his various measures in the Eastern Provinces to protect national rights and resist economic aggression cannot be said to have been without considerable effort. We can see from the Japanese' relentless efforts to exclude and discredit Zhang, and their public declaration that they would never allow Zhang to return to Manchuria, that the key lies in something self-evident. What the enemy wants to destroy is what we should cherish. This is my personal opinion. In this conference, the representatives' election of Zhang to jointly shoulder responsibility, I imagine, is also based on this opinion. Patriotic citizens should also encourage Zhang to strive forward with expectation, he said. (24th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Yan Huiqing Arrived in Nanjing Yesterday 34

Scheduled to Set Sail on the 27th

(Nanjing) Yan Huiqing arrived in Nanjing on the morning of the 24th. He first visited Gu Weijun at the Huilong Hotel to discuss the Sino-Japanese issue for half an hour. Then he went to his younger brother Yan Deqing's residence to rest. At 2 p.m., he bid farewell to Chiang. They had a long discussion about future diplomatic strategies and his mission after going to the United States. Yan told visitors that regarding the Sino-Japanese issue, the League of Nations recently complied with the Japanese request to form an international investigation team. Our country naturally opposes this kind of investigation team, which would delay the withdrawal of troops, unless the Japanese first withdraw their troops. The purpose that the Japanese hope to achieve with the investigation team is to deceive the members of the team and hope to have their dispatch of troops recognized as legitimate. Our country believes that the current situation in the Northeast is extremely dangerous, and a disaster may erupt at any time. If the fuse is not removed first, then the investigation is an investigation, and the forcible occupation is a forcible occupation. What good is it to the facts? The League of Nations should not accept this. I have already purchased a ship ticket and will go to Shanghai on the 26th and set sail on the 27th. It is expected that when I arrive in the United States, it will be the time when the United States Congress is in session, and perhaps a fair review of the Sino-Japanese incident can be heard. I still need to meet with Mr. Wu Ti Yun when I pass through Shanghai, he said. (24th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Secretary Li Chang and Chief Officer Yan Rongsheng are accompanying Yan to the United States this time. His family is not traveling with him. (24th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Acting Foreign Minister Gu Weijun is scheduled to take office in the next day or two. Because it is an acting position, there may be no inauguration ceremony. (24th Dispatch)

Sorting Out Financial Bonds Fundraising to Begin Soon 41

Guangdong Fourth Plenary Session Splits 46

Xiao and Deng Contact Factionalists

The Conference Overturns the Shanghai Meeting Proposals

Sun, Chen and Li Consider this a Vote of No Confidence

They Exit the Conference to Hong Kong

(Hong Kong) Sun Ke, Chen Youren, and Li Wenfan left the province for Hong Kong on the 24th, along with twenty other representatives to the Fourth Plenary Session. (24th Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Because the opinions of the representatives to the Fourth Plenary Session were inconsistent, Sun Ke visited Chen Jitang three times to negotiate, but Chen claimed illness and refused to see him. When the Fourth Plenary Session opened on the 23rd, Sun and Chen did not attend. After the resolution to overturn the Shanghai Conference was passed, Sun, Li, and Chen considered the conference to be a vote of no confidence in them and decided to withdraw from the conference and report to Shanghai by telegram. On the morning of the 24th, they came to Hong Kong with northern representatives Zhao Pilian, Guo Chuntao, Bai Yunti, and dozens of others. Sun, Li, and Chen decided to go to Macau on the 25th and then transfer to Zhongshan County for temporary residence. Jing Tingyi, Zhang Zhiben, Liang Hancao, and others also withdrew from the Fourth Plenary Session. This disturbance was initiated by the power faction and Xiao Focheng, Deng Ziru, and others. They are now telegraphing Hu, urging him to return to Guangdong to preside over the situation. (24th Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Sun Ke, Li Wenfan, and Chen Youren sent a letter to the Fourth Plenary Session from Hong Kong on the 24th, first stating the results of the peace talks: 1. To promote the unity of the party and the unity of the country; 2. To determine the reform of the future political system. Among them, the most important is to reassemble the cadres of the first, second, and third central committees to give the party new life. If the decisions of the peace talks can be implemented one by one, then dictatorship will naturally not occur. Advocating an extraordinary conference is consistent with this idea. Next, they defended the election of members of the first, second, and third central committees as members of the fourth central committee, which the conference considered to be in violation of the party charter. They said that the party has been in turmoil for several years, and it is impossible to resolve it entirely based on the party charter. We cannot use the party charter to erase all facts. Even if the extraordinary conference has no basis in the party charter, the fourth plenary session convened by the extraordinary conference also has no basis. How can we respond to this? They continued that one of the most important parts of the peace talks has been rejected, then the prospects for party unity and national unity have been greatly hampered. Ke, Fan, Ren and others are representatives of the peace talks, how can they bear this important responsibility lightly? They can only withdraw from the conference and quietly await the public judgment of comrades and citizens. Finally, they said that Wang and Hu are united in good faith and working for the country with all their hearts. They hope that their comrades will overturn the previous resolution and accept the proposals of the extraordinary conference, then it is not too late to mend the fold. Also, Bai Yunti said that since we are not succumbed by dictatorship, how can we be insulted by separatism? A total of one hundred representatives to the Fourth Plenary Session came to Hong Kong on the 24th. The entire left wing withdrew. The Guangdong Fourth Plenary Session will issue a declaration to explain the resolution of the 23rd, in order to avoid outsiders suspecting that it hinders the progress of unification. On the 24th, the price of medium paper fell from 91 to 83. (24th Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Fourth Plenary Session is scheduled to hold its third meeting on the 25th to discuss foreign affairs and military issues. (24th Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Chen Jitang sent Chen Zhangfu to inspect the defense on the northeast suburbs on the 24th. (24th Dispatch)

Generals from the First Army Group have been volunteering to aid Heilongjiang. (24th Dispatch)

Wu resigned and left, and the National Government's Military Counselor Office sent someone to accompany him to pay his respects at Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum. After returning to his residence, he resumed eating. (24th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Foreign News

The Japanese Cabinet Shows Signs of Wavering 76

Adachi Advocates Organizing a Coalition Cabinet

The Government and Parties Form a Head-On Conflict

Dentsu News Agency, Tokyo, 24th - The conflict between the government and parties is becoming increasingly complex. The status quo maintenance faction centered on Prime Minister Wakatsuki and the coalition faction advocated by Interior Minister Adachi have begun vigorous efforts. One side is making every effort to prevent its realization, while the other side is actively working to establish a plan. The head-on confrontation is as incompatible as fire and water, and the disintegration of the cabinet is inevitable.

Another dispatch: The attitudes of various senior statesmen towards the coalition cabinet advocated by Interior Minister Adachi are currently calm, but many believe that Wakatsuki's claims and Adachi's advances are too biased. The Wakatsuki's non-partisan cabinet has considerable reasons, but they do not want to change the current situation regarding the coalition cabinet issue.

Another dispatch: Finance Minister Inoue met with Wakatsuki at 4:30 PM yesterday to discuss the coalition cabinet issue advocated by Adachi. He strongly opposed it, believing that the foundations would be shaken during this autumn of financial and diplomatic difficulties, and he hoped that Adachi would reflect and avoid affecting the overall situation.

Another dispatch: Interior Minister Adachi met with advisors Tomita and Matsuda, and Director-General Raiki yesterday and made an important statement as follows: The success or failure of realizing the coalition cabinet depends on future efforts. Those who oppose a non-partisan cabinet united by the whole country should be regarded as unpatriotic.

Russia Changes to a Five-Day Rest System 77

Regulating Five Days of Rest Each Month

Kokumin News Agency, Moscow, 23rd - Last year, for the convenience of implementing the Five-Year Plan, the Soviet Union had a regulation of every five days being a week. Now, this regulation has been explicitly abolished by the People's Committee. The new order stipulates that from December 1st, six days will be a week, and each will have one day of rest after a week of work. Subsequently, the 6th, 12th, 18th, 24th, and 28th of each month will be rest days for all factories and government agencies.

In addition, nineteen young male and female radical writers were shot by the Chinese authorities in front of Li's grave. The Nanjing government should not cruelly kill Chinese scholars, etc.

News Highlights

The Fall of Longjiang and its Aftermath 81

Ma Zhanshan Leads Troops in Fierce Battle for Two Days and Nights

Soldiers Fight Bravely Against the Enemy, Depleted of Support and Ammunition

On the 19th, Retreat to Keshan with Plans for Counterattack

Harbin Communication, Republic of China Year 10, November 19th. Ma Zhanshan, with his isolated army without support, exhausted of ammunition and strength, was defeated and retreated to Keshan. The city of Heilongjiang Province, belonging to our territory and under our government, is being watched by 400 million compatriots and 2 million soldiers as it falls to a foreign race. I, foolishly drafting this communication now, am heartbroken and do not know whether it is ink or tears.

Preparation of the Japanese before the Great Battle. Since November 4th, the Heilongjiang army has repeatedly crushed strong enemies. The Kwantung Japanese Army, with all its 8,000 troops, attacked several times but were repelled. Therefore, Honjo Shigeru was furious and secretly requested instructions from his government. His memorial to the Chief of the General Staff stated, (Regarding the military situation in Heilongjiang, it has reached a state of extreme evil. The Kwantung Garrison has come to believe that the time has come to make a final decision to defeat it. For strategic convenience, certain locations should be occupied so that our army (Japanese army) can defeat the many with the few. If we always act according to the will of the government, opportunities will be lost. Please grant the Kwantung Army Commander the authority to make independent decisions in emergencies, and please approve this intention.) With the plan to attack Heilongjiang finalized, Honjo issued a final ultimatum to Ma Zhanshan in his name at 8:30 AM on the 16th. The original text stated, (I have received an urgent telegram from Minister of the Army Minami in the Ministry of the Army, making three demands on Ma Zhanshan: (1) The Ma army must withdraw north to Qiqihar. All troops concentrated in Qiqihar and Ang'angxi must be returned to their original locations immediately. (2) The Ma army must not be stationed south of the Chinese Eastern Railway. (3) Ma must not interfere with the management of the Tao'ang Railway Bureau. Otherwise, the Japanese army will immediately take necessary and effective measures. Regarding the above three points, they must be implemented within ten days from November 14th. After all conditions are met, the Japanese army may consider withdrawing the Nenjiang Detachment. A reply is required by noon today (the 16th), to be forwarded by the Japanese Special Service Agency in Harbin.) After receiving this unreasonable demand, Ma immediately reported the information to Zhang Xueliang and requested instructions on how to deal with it. Zhang telegraphed a detailed refutation: (1) Qiqihar and Ang'angxi are entirely Chinese territory, and the Ma Zhanshan army is a Chinese government army. On what basis does the Japanese government interfere with their stationing within their own country? It is highly inappropriate. (2) Both north and south of the Chinese Eastern Railway are Chinese territory. Why should the Japanese army forcibly withdraw and change its garrison location? (3) The Tao'ang Railway was built with a Japanese loan, but the loan contract clearly stipulates that the sovereignty of the railway belongs entirely to our country. All management and control cannot be unilaterally controlled by the creditor. This is recognized by all countries in the world and is a completely unreasonable demand that cannot be accepted.) Before the Japanese ultimatum arrived, the Korean 8th Mixed Brigade had already been formed and dispatched. On the 16th of this month, trains between Shenyang and Changchun on the South Manchuria Railway were stopped for half a day. It was rumored that bandits were disturbing the railway at Fanjiatun, causing transportation disruptions. In reality, the Japanese were trying to free up space to transport troops from the 8th Mixed Brigade. The two regiments of cavalry artillery from that unit arrived in Taonan on the evening of the 17th. Thus, the battle began at about 10 PM that night.

Two Days and Nights of Bloody Battle by Our Army. The Japanese army, well-prepared, divided into two forces for frontal and flank attacks. The Hasebe Brigade and the Lushun Heavy Artillery Regiment, totaling about 4,000 troops, attacked the first line of defense at Daxing Station, Sanjianfang, Xiaosanjiazi, Daguantun, etc., pressing from the front and preventing our army from moving. Meanwhile, the newly arrived Korean Mixed Brigade, with two cavalry regiments, plus a portion of the Domon Division's infantry and artillery, and all of the Amano Brigade's cavalry and infantry, totaling more than 7,000 troops, with four tanks attached, bypassed the northern end of Jiangqiao and attacked the left flank of our cavalry on the third line of defense at Tangchi Mushroom Creek. Defending that area were the 1st regiment of Cheng Zhiyuan's 8th Cavalry Brigade, the 1st regiment of Ma Zhanshan's guards, and the Shali Township Regiment of Wu Songshan's 1st Cavalry Brigade, totaling three regiments. However, after repeated casualties, no more than 2,000 men remained. The enemy attacked with a force several times larger, with extremely fierce artillery fire. Our army was outnumbered, but the soldiers were loyal to the country and did not flinch because of their small numbers. From the start of the firing at ten o'clock, the battle was extremely fierce. Our army resisted with all its might, defending from the trenches. Enemy cavalry battalions charged more than ten times, but were repelled by our effective use of mortars and machine guns. After three hours, the enemy's tanks had approached our trenches, covering infantry machine gun teams. Bullets rained down, and wooden stakes and iron nets outside the trenches were destroyed. Many trenches were collapsed, and each regiment and battalion was forced into dozens of separate locations by machine gun and artillery fire. At the same time, Japanese cavalry surrounded from the left rear. Our army could no longer stand in the trenches, and fought outside the trenches after four o'clock. However, the ranks had already been scattered, and most of the horses had been blown up. The regimental commander Tu Quansheng still bravely shouted and led his two cavalry companies and one infantry squad to charge into the enemy lines five times. The enemy cavalry retreated several times to avoid them. By five o'clock in the morning, our army had no reinforcements, and ammunition was running out. The gun barrels were all heated and could no longer be used. Seven Japanese planes also assisted in the attack from the air, dropping hundreds of heavy bombs. At this point, almost none of our soldiers were intact, but they still fought bravely, retreating to Hongqiyingzi in hopes of receiving reinforcements from that direction and cooperating in a counterattack. Unexpectedly, the infantry in that area was also pressing tightly from the front, rushing to provide support. At this point, Tu Quansheng had no choice but to lead the remaining 700 soldiers, breaking through the firing line and retreating to Ang'angxi at about ten o'clock, blocking the railway to resist the enemy. Japanese planes and cavalry artillery continued to attack fiercely, and many shells fell on the tracks of the Eastern Railway. After holding out until noon, Chairman Ma Zhanshan rushed from the provincial capital to encourage the soldiers and personally led the pistol team as a vanguard, launching a fierce counterattack. After a strong attack, the enemy was driven back at about two o'clock in the afternoon, and the original defense was restored at half past two. The flank battle ended at this point. The battle on the front line at Daxing Station, Xinlitu, and Sanjianfang occurred at 10:40 PM. The Japanese army immediately attacked with 4,000 troops, first harassing our left and right wings with cavalry, and then attacking the front of Sanjianfang with infantry and artillery. Initially, the intention was to contain us, preventing us from rushing to aid the flanks, so the attack was not yet fierce. After two o'clock on the morning of the 18th, the troops were increased, and eight tanks and more than thirty artillery pieces were used to attack fiercely. Our army had only three flat-trajectory guns, which were used to resist their tanks. The enemy's advantage was slightly repelled, but the guns and artillery fired continuously, and the pressure gradually increased. Our artillery was not able to withstand the long range, and the soldiers only used rifles to resist. The resistance was naturally weak. At 3:20, the Xinlitu defense line was the first to be broken. The troops in that area retreated to Daxing Station, and with the assistance of the artillery, they launched two fierce attacks and recaptured the position at about four o'clock. However, not long after, the Daguantun defense line was again surrounded by the enemy. Zhang Brigade's cavalry was trapped in the trenches, and the situation was already critical. Wu Songshan's unit assisted Yuan Brigade in a rescue operation at five o'clock, relieving the siege. Since then, the situation has become even more dangerous, and the position has been lost and recaptured several times. After holding out until ten o'clock, twelve Japanese planes and twelve tanks attacked, and at the same time, a regiment of new Korean troops arrived to join the fierce attack. The Japanese army attacking our Tangchi Mushroom Creek, taking advantage of their victory, circled around from our rear. Our army on the third line of defense, with less than 2,000 men, was originally only a link between the first and second lines of defense. It was difficult to stand firm under the enemy's attack, so it gathered at the first line of defense. The enemy's encirclement having been completed, they unleashed the power of both air and land forces, attacking from above, below, front, and back. Since the night battle on the 17th, ammunition had been cut off. People and horses had not eaten for a day and a night. The mountain guns and flat-trajectory guns had also run out of ammunition due to firing too many shells, so they switched to using mortars to bombard the enemy's dense formations. However, the enemy, relying on the power of the tanks, was not afraid at all. At two o'clock in the afternoon, the trenches were completely destroyed. More than half of the Yuan and Wu Brigades had died. A battalion of Zhang Dianjiu's unit, with ammunition running out, was the first to break through and retreat. The other units were affected, and it became increasingly difficult to defend. The officers and soldiers left the trenches one after another, cutting a path to the rear. Due to the lack of ammunition, they even engaged in hand-to-hand combat with gun stocks. The enemy charged with bayonets, and countless of our soldiers fought to the death. At 4:30, they were unable to resist the enemy any longer and retreated to Hongqiyingzi. During the most intense battle, a mortar soldier named Pang Zhenhai from the 4th Regiment of the 1st Cavalry Brigade fired more than eighty shells. Suddenly, the firing pin broke. He still shouted and killed with his bare hands. His comrades pulled him out of the trench, but he became so agitated that he went insane. Barefoot and naked, he rushed to the enemy lines, and other soldiers had to drag him back by force.

The Inevitable Retreat to Keshan. In the urgency of the situation, Chairman Ma Zhanshan repeatedly telegraphed various parties for assistance. The Jilin army watched without moving. The authorities in Beiping also gave no definite instructions. Ma borrowed ammunition from Ding Chao in Harbin, but Ding refused. Since the Tao'ang Railway battle, the bullets used were all old stocks from Heilongjiang Province, and most were moldy and unusable. After a day and night of fierce fighting, nine out of ten rounds had been used up. The soldiers had fighting spirit, but what could they do when they were unable to fight back with their bare hands? Seeing that the front line was already hopeless, Ma issued a general retreat order at six o'clock on the afternoon of the 18th. All the main forces retreated along the Qiqihar-Ang'angxi Railway to the provincial capital, leaving the cavalry to set up a defensive line at Wuma Place, 18 miles from the city (Qiqihar-Ang'angxi Railway Station). At that time, the provincial capital was already in chaos. A separate detachment of the Japanese army, with four to five hundred cavalrymen as one branch, bypassed the Chinese Eastern Railway from Jingxing, passing through Gan Jingzi, Jixin River, and Lindian, to attack the provincial capital. Ma divided his troops to block them. After ten o'clock in the evening, the situation became increasingly tense. The Japanese army advanced from Hongqiyingzi towards the provincial capital. The provincial capital had no defenses to hold. Ma then issued another order to move the provincial government to Keshan County. All provincial government officials who were willing to go were escorted in retreat by Yuan Chonggu's brigade. Ma himself still led his guard force of more than 500 men and more than 700 cavalry to guard Longsha. That night, Ma spoke to Zhang Jinghui and Ding Chao in Harbin via long-distance telephone, instructing them to convey to the Japanese army not to harm the people of Heilongjiang. At nine o'clock on the morning of the 19th, a large part of the Japanese army crossed the Chinese Eastern Railway line from the Tianqiao on the Tao'ang Railway, stopping at Yushutun, fifteen miles outside the Black Wall. At 9:20, they attacked our army at Wuma Place. Ma Zhanshan mobilized the entire city to fight, reinforcing the defending troops there. The Japanese army still used planes to drop bombs, and two planes flew over the city, dropping twenty bombs, destroying one military and civilian government office and one house each, causing fierce fires. A part of the Japanese army cavalry appeared at the Qiqihar-Keshan Railway Station, attacking the rear of our army and civilians. Seeing that the situation was hopeless, Ma entered the city to bundle up important documents from various agencies and protect a part of the merchants and civilians, retreating along the Qiqihar-Keshan Railway. Thousands of merchants, civilians, the elderly, children, and personnel from various agencies followed, and the situation was extremely miserable. When retreating, in order to prevent the Japanese army from pursuing, a section of the Qiqihar-Taianzhen railway tracks was destroyed. Keshan is ninety Chinese miles from the Black Wall, and Taianzhen is sixty miles from the Black Wall. It is heard that Ma's plan is to gather the people's militia in Keshan and try to counterattack. If the Japanese army continues to press on, or if time does not allow, then he will retreat to Baiquan and train the people's militia.

The Soviet Russian Attitude is Extremely Silent. On the morning of the 19th, the Japanese army sent a team of soldiers to the Ang'angxi station of the Chinese Eastern Railway to monitor the railway staff and special police and railway police. Station staff entering and leaving must wear armbands. During the fierce fighting on the 18th, the Japanese army dropped many bombs on the Ang'angxi station, destroying railway tracks and sleepers. The Soviet Russian government made no comment, and the Russian personnel of the Chinese Eastern Railway also acted as if they did not see it. Although the Japanese army withdrew from Ang'angxi on the afternoon of the 19th, a large number of Japanese troops were still stationed at the Ang'angxi station of the Tao'ang Railway (eight Chinese miles from the Chinese Eastern Railway station), and the Russian side made no statement. It is heard that the Japanese Consul General in Harbin, O Hashimoto Chuichi, sent a public letter to the Russian Director of the Chinese Eastern Railway on the night of the 18th, so the Russian side considered it satisfactory. The original text is as follows: (The Japanese army's challenge to Ma Zhanshan's army concentrated in the area south of Ang'angxi is a measure of self-defense and has to resort to war. The commander of the Kwantung Army has ordered the commander of the first line of troops to respect the interests of the Chinese Eastern Railway, and also said that if the railway protection army does not take hostile actions, the Japanese side will not attack. However, in the future, in the progress of the war, Ma Zhanshan's army may use the terrain and objects near the Chinese Eastern Railway, or take military actions to retreat within the area, which will inevitably damage the property of the Chinese Eastern Railway. At this critical moment, it is urgent for your railway to seriously advise Ma Zhanshan's army not to take the above actions. In order to protect the property of your railway, I dare to inform you of the above. Addressed to Lodeevsky Li Shaogeng. Hashimoto Chuichi, Japanese Consul General in Harbin, November 18th.) As for the security of Harbin, it is still under our country's jurisdiction at present. However, with Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang successively falling, Harbin, with its small area, is isolated in the middle, and it may be difficult to survive alone. However, whether the Japanese will send troops to Harbin, or order the officials and clerks in Harbin to fly the Japanese flag and implement martial law to inspect mail and telegraphs, is still a question. As for the Japanese army, at half past ten on the afternoon of the 19th, they first sent more than a hundred cavalrymen, in several small teams, to enter the Black Wall to search. Seeing that there was no movement, they stopped at the consulate. At one o'clock in the afternoon, a Japanese plane circled over the Black Wall, distributing Domon's absurd proclamations, which stated, (Our army has been forced to fight with the Chinese Heilongjiang army. The target is the enemy. I will never disturb the Chinese Eastern Railway and Qiqihar Station, and I am willing to have friendly relations with the local people and authorities. In the future, if troops are needed to stay in the provincial capital of Jiang Province, I do not want to interfere in local internal affairs, so I hope that those who do not hinder my army's actions will continue to work as usual.) At three o'clock in the afternoon, Domon led a part of the army into the city, staying at the Longjiang Hotel, and sent troops to extinguish the flames of the provincial border office. In the evening, two regiments of cavalry and infantry entered and occupied the three major camps in the east, south, and north. Another part of the army camped outside the city, and more than 3,000 cavalry pursued our army along the Qiqihar-Keshan Railway. However, the retreat of the Heilongjiang army was very methodical. On the evening of the 19th, Bu Brigade Yuan Chonggu set off for Baiquan. The people's militias in Heilongjiang, Dongqinggang, Suihua, and other places, upon hearing the news, rose up to support Ma, and telegraphed Ma to retreat to Baiquan, and that the joint force would provide support. Therefore, last night, the Japanese army stopped near Taianzhen and did not dare to advance. Merchants and civilians in Heilongjiang Province closed their businesses completely on the 18th. For the past two days, they have not yet resumed business. The Japanese army forced them to hang Japanese flags to welcome them. Many merchants and civilians, fearing the threat of the Japanese army, fled to Harbin. The passenger trains from Ang'angxi to Harbin last night were all packed with men and women seeking refuge. Today, there are still a large number of refugees waiting for trains in Ang'angxi. Last night, seven robbery cases occurred in the Black Wall, all committed by Korean vagrants. The Japanese army turned a blind eye. The Chamber of Commerce, because the police had withdrawn with the army, specially formed a temporary merchant corps yesterday to maintain order. The Japanese plan was originally to make Zhang Haipeng the chairman of Heilongjiang. Recently, because Zhang killed the Japanese who were monitoring the Zhang army, he has become an enemy of the Japanese. On the evening of the 19th, Zhang also led his troops to disrupt the Tao'ang line, destroying the railway tracks between Tailai and Taonan, and clashed with the Japanese army. Therefore, the Japanese army had to look for someone else. In recent days, the Japanese Consul in Harbin, Black and Forest Hide, the representative of Honjo, repeatedly forced Zhang Jinghui to go to the Black Wall to serve as chairman, and Ding Chao of the Railway Protection Army replaced Zhang as the chief of the special zone. Yesterday afternoon, the Chinese Eastern Railway and Qiqihar-Ang'angxi railways prepared a special car for Zhang, but he did not depart at the appointed time. He will go at three o'clock this afternoon. As for Ding Chao, he was originally a classmate of Xi Haxia. After Xi became independent, he appointed him as commander of the Railway Protection Army. At the same time, Zhang Zuoxiang also telegraphed Ding to act as his agent. After Ding took office, he straddled the fence for a long time. Recently, through Zhang Jinghui's mediation, he has reached a tacit understanding with the Japanese. Therefore, when the Heilongjiang army begged for help on the 18th and 19th, Ding held several brigades of the Jilin army and watched without moving. He also ordered the Railway Protection Army at the Ang'angxi station not to oppose the Japanese army when it passed through. On the 19th, when the Japanese army passed through the Ang'angxi station, Ding's troops hung Chinese and Japanese flags to show no resistance. All of this shows the leopard's transformation in the current situation and the rise and fall of slave patriots. (12:00 noon on the 20th)

The Secrets Before Pu Yi Left the Customs 82

Talked About by Pu's Followers

Beiping Communication. This time, Pu Yi was taken to Guanwai by Doihara Kenji and Zheng Xiaoxu, etc., and the Japanese will use him as the protagonist of the independence of the three northeastern provinces, which is undoubtedly beyond doubt. However, what is Pu Yi's personal will? Until now, everyone has different opinions. Now, Mr. Hu, who accompanied Pu Yi to play tennis in Tianjin for five years, came to Ping today and talked about Pu Yi's usual behavior and the recent events. Pu Yi's attitude can at least be known in most cases. Mr. Hu said, I have been with Pu Yi for five years and observed his behavior. He is a stupid and昏庸person. He usually has a very bad temper. Even if his teachers Chen Baochen and Zheng Xiaoxu slightly offended him, he would scold them. Chen and others would kowtow and cry to persuade him, but they were never heard. Pu Yi has very close relations with the Japanese. He likes to eat Japanese sashimi and authentic sake, and he tries his best to imitate Western habits, wearing Western clothes and leather shoes, and speaking broken English, thinking he is very happy. He also has a love for boys and keeps as many as twenty-five of them. Among them, Wang Xiaosan is the most favored. He is as charming as a prostitute and never leaves for a moment. As far as I know, the rewards Wang has received are more than 100,000. These boys all live on the third floor, indulging in lewdness day and night, and the filth is spreading everywhere. He is very indifferent to his wives and concubines because of the encirclement of the boys. His wife, Rong, is a modern woman who is good at dancing and singing, and is very lively. She occasionally gets Pu Yi's favor. As for his concubine, Jin Wenxiu, she is an old-fashioned woman, very restrained and good at crying, and Pu Yi hates her even more. After being provoked, Pu once issued an edict saying, (You deceive the king, and your crime deserves death. I will give you death), etc. Wenxiu was even more afraid, and she was not tolerated by the wife, so she divorced. Pu spent 190,000 yuan on this matter, and Wenxiu only received 50,000. His昏瞆and muddleheadedness can be known. Pu respects the Englishman Reginald Johnston the most, because he also believes in Europeanization. After the Eastern Province Incident, the Japanese side sent a person named Kageyama to live in his house to guard it. All those who visited had to get his consent. At the beginning of the month, Doihara came to Tianjin with Jin Liang, Zheng Xiaoxu, and Zheng's son Zheng Yu, etc., to encourage Pu Yi to leave the customs. When Zai Tao and Chen Baochen heard about it, they strongly opposed it, saying that the Japanese were only using this to scare the Nanjing government and make it soften. They were not really helping. If they were fooled, it would be very dangerous in the future. It is better to temporarily go to Beiping to ensure safety. They also discussed with the Ping authorities, planning to take the opportunity to take Pu Yi to Ping to avoid being surrounded by the Japanese. The Ping authorities also agreed with their statement and had found a house next to the American Embassy in Dongjiaomin Lane for Pu Yi to live in, and promised to send a special car to Tianjin to pick him up. However, Doihara and Jin Liang, etc., knew about it, so they used tricks to send gifts, secretly placing bombs to scare him. Pu Yi was really caught in the trap, and was panic-stricken. On the 8th, the plainclothes team launched an incident, and there was a lot of gunfire. Jin Liang, Doihara, Zheng Xiaoxu, and his son Zheng Hao thought that the opportunity had come, so they greeted Pu Yi in an armored car, falsely saying that Tianjin would be in great chaos and that the Japanese concession would become the focus of artillery fire. It is better to avoid it early and go to the Japanese consul's residence in the British concession to seek safety. Pu Yi was taken away in panic and confusion. The next day, he boarded a Japanese warship from the Japanese Consul's residence and went to Dalian. Zheng Xiaoxu and his son also followed. As for the details of the agreement with the Japanese, nothing is known. The rumors from the outside are mostly speculation. It is heard that Pu's wife, Rong, knew in advance that Pu intended to agree to leave the customs and tried to dissuade him. Pu said angrily, (Living here, I am just a citizen of Tianjin. When I get to Guanwai, even if I am the second Joseon, I will be a hundred times more glorious and wealthy than being a commoner). Therefore, judging from Pu Yi's daily behavior and his recent statements, it can be concluded that he is willing to be a Japanese puppet. (22nd)

Students Petition to Go to Beijing. Temporary Court Organized for Riot Case. The case of the Wuyi County merchants' riot, destroying the Party Headquarters and other three organizations, and beating Wen Bi to death, has been prosecuted by the County Court Procuratorate for the criminal part. As for the reactionary part, it has been approved by the High Court to form a temporary court according to law, which is the responsibility of the County Government. Today's news, County Mayor Zhang has sent a letter to the County Court to retrieve the files, and has applied to the High Court to send personnel to organize the court.

Nantong 85

Advocating the Use of Tongzhou Native Cloth. Tongzhou large-sized native cloth was sold exclusively to the three northeastern provinces and Jiangbei Li Xiahe. Since Guanwai has fallen and there is a major flood in the lower reaches of the river, the sale of cloth has been greatly affected. The local people from all walks of life are now appealing to the province and ministry to advocate its use to save the cloth industry.

Xiaoshan 86

Agricultural Association Estimates of Field Industry are Unsatisfactory. The previous unilateral estimates of the yield of fields and crops by the rural agricultural associations in Xiaoshan County were mostly unsatisfactory to the owners. In addition, the collection fee of one dime and two cents per mu further increased the burden on the farmers. Now both the tenants and the owners have jointly filed complaints with the provincial and county governments, so there will inevitably be a dispute when the rent payment period arrives this year.

Local News

Yesterday's Shanghai City Universities and Middle Schools - Students Petitioned in Beijing 89

Students from various universities marched in different areas in the morning to show support

Over 8,000 students gathered at the North Station in the afternoon to depart

The fifth and final group fully departed at 1:15 AM this morning

All teams were orderly and their emotions were exceptionally somber and heroic

—The purpose of this trip is to request the government to send troops to resist Japan immediately—

The Anti-Japanese and National Salvation Joint Associations of Universities and Middle Schools in this city, in view of the increasing national crisis and the relentless attacks by the brutal Japanese forces, and the lack of united resistance from our government and people, which is insufficient to save the nation from destruction, the Joint Associations of Universities and Middle Schools organized a delegation to urge the government to send troops. It was decided that yesterday at 3 PM, over 40 schools, totaling over 10,000 people, would gather at the North Railway Station to depart. Many welcoming teams from various schools, representatives from various organizations, and people from all walks of life came to see them off. The petitioners were neatly dressed, full of spirit, and in unprecedented order. Around 5 PM, they divided into teams and boarded trains to go to the capital. The crowd shouted slogans such as "We swear not to return until our goal is achieved," and their somber indignation was moving. Students from various universities also marched in different areas yesterday morning to boost their momentum. The details of the march and departure to the capital are as follows:

(I) Marching Circumstances 90

Southern City Area 91

The university students marched for: (1) to support the students who went to Beijing to petition, in order to achieve the final goal, and to express the determination and strength of all Shanghai students; (2) to oppose the unreasonable atrocities and insults by Japanese soldiers against legitimate patriotic movements within Chinese territory; (3) to give a serious expression regarding the current situation, the League of Nations, and the Japanese invasion of Heilongjiang. Therefore, at 9 AM yesterday, students from various universities held separate marches in different areas to support the petition to Beijing. The Southern City area departed from the West Gate Public Stadium, with Xu Banghe of Jiaotong University as the general commander and Wu Zemin of Daxia University as the chief disciplinarian. Jinan University Leading the Way 97

There were three to four hundred petitioners from Jinan University. The school anticipated heavy traffic and overcrowding when all schools gathered, so they left early in the morning. They took the Beijing-Shanghai train around 7 AM and arrived at Xiaguan at 4 PM, waiting for the Shanghai university students to gather before going to the National Government to petition.

A Glimpse of the North Station 98

Around 2 PM, students from various schools arrived by moving trucks. The students from each school wore volunteer army uniforms and held petition flags, with slogans such as "Request the government to recover lost territories" and "Punish the negligent officials in the Northeast." By the time, several thousand people had arrived, crowding the platform and station. Flags fluttered and military music played. The petitioners were all spirited and filled with grief and anger.

Five Departures 99

Students from various schools arrived at the North Station one after another around 2 PM. Those who lived farther away arrived by moving trucks and lined up in the open space in front of the station before entering the platform and boarding the train in order. They boarded the Tongkuai train to Beijing via Zhabei at 3:15 PM. However, the train had limited carriages. There were over 8,000 students who arrived at the station, and the Railway Bureau only allowed seven additional carriages, which was still insufficient. Therefore, none of the teams boarded the train and waited on the platform. At the same time, the general command gathered representatives from various schools and held an emergency meeting in the waiting room of the station. It was decided to send eight representatives to negotiate with the Transportation Department. After several discussions, no results were achieved. It wasn't until around 5 PM that the Railway Bureau reluctantly mobilized carriages, stopped selling tickets, and allocated the originally scheduled number of passenger cars to the students. They were divided into five trains. The first train departed at 5:33 PM, the second at 6:27 PM, the third at 6:55 PM, the fourth at around 10 PM, and the fifth at 1:15 AM this morning. At the same time, schools along the way, such as Suzhou, Wuxi, and Changzhou, also joined, totaling over 5,000 people. The total number was over 14,000 people.

Condition of the Passenger Cars 100

When representatives from various schools negotiated with the Railway Bureau, and the Railway Bureau claimed that there were no cars available, the Zaokuai train and Tongche train from Beijing to Shanghai were about to arrive at the North Station. The Railway Bureau, fearing that the students would occupy the trains, hurriedly ordered the Maigen Road Station to hold the two trains and drive them into the storage track. The trains that were supposed to depart from Shanghai were also suspended as a result. All ticket offices stopped selling tickets and displayed "Sold Out." Only after the trains carrying the students from various schools had departed did the Zaokuai train from Beijing, which had been stopped at Maigen Road, release to the North Station. The Tongkuai train also arrived in Shanghai and switched tracks to Hangzhou. The Yekuai train from Shanghai to Beijing still departed as usual, but the departure time was much later than originally scheduled.

Pan Chuji, Guan Zhaowei, and Yang Shouchang from Shanghai News Agency, Ji Youfei and others from Riri News Agency.

The delegation of university representatives held its fourth emergency meeting in the waiting room of the North Station at 2 PM yesterday. Zhou Xiaobo of Fudan University presided over the meeting. (3) The orders of the delegation would be conveyed by the director of the secretariat to the general commander. Command Outline 103

(1) The order of the teams from each school remains as previously stipulated; (2) The assembly address is in front of the old Wusong Railway Station; (3) The order of boarding the train should follow the original order of the teams; (4) After getting off the train, the teams should line up according to their order and listen to the orders of the general commander; (5) Walk into the city; (6) Each commander should assemble upon hearing the horn; (7) Stand in front of the National Government and listen to the orders of the general commander; (8) Each school should not blow horns, but use military whistles for assembly, and the following disciplinary regulations are stipulated: (1) Absolutely obey orders; (2) Be able to endure hardship; (3) Help each other; (4) Strive for neatness in the ranks; (5) Strive for cleanliness in clothing; (6) Strive for simplicity in luggage; (7) Do not leave the ranks without permission; (8) Do not rush to occupy seats; (9) Do not talk and laugh arbitrarily; (10) Do not express opinions arbitrarily.

Document to Chairman Chiang 104

The Anti-Japanese and National Salvation United Association of Students of Shanghai Universities presented a document to Chairman Chiang to urge the government to send troops: Presented to urge the Japanese invaders to become increasingly urgent, the national situation is in danger, and a special delegation has been sent to appeal to you to follow the situation and immediately send troops to recover the lost land in the Northeast to maintain the survival of the nation. Since September 18, when the Japanese imperialists, disregarding the great injustice of the world, invaded and occupied Liaoning and Jilin, the local officials in the Northeast adopted a policy of non-resistance, retreating step by step, which was absurd and perverse, and shocked the whole country. The students were filled with righteous indignation and formed teams in late September to appeal for troops to be sent to resist the invaders and avenge the humiliation. At that time, you publicly declared that the lost land would be recovered in the shortest possible time, and that if the Japanese soldiers advanced any further, they would be met with a head-on blow. The students believed that you held an important position in the country and that your word was as good as gold, and that you would have something to comfort the people. Therefore, we obeyed the order and returned to Shanghai, on the one hand, to intensify our studies in preparation for a long-term struggle, and on the other hand, to carry out military training to serve as a backup for the government. However, more than a month has passed, and not only has not a single inch of the lost land been recovered, but the invaders' flames have grown and the invaders' atmosphere has become more intense. After the disturbances in Tianjin and Tianjin, followed by the fall of Heilongjiang Province, they even attacked Jinzhou, entering homes and ascending halls, and the country is facing destruction every day. However, the government's self-defense and sending of troops has not yet been shown in fact. The students have been holding their composure for too long, and their boiling blood is unbearable. Therefore, we have sent 5,000 students to organize a delegation, with a very orderly spirit and a firm attitude, to appeal to you again, one, to personally write a mobilization speech to the public immediately, stating in the speech that you will personally lead the troops to depart north immediately, no later than December 1, and will not return to Beijing until the lost land is recovered; and two, to strictly order Zhang Xueliang to send troops immediately to recover the lost land, and if there is still no indication of sending troops within three days, he will be dismissed and severely punished. The delegation represents the will of all Shanghai students, is entrusted by all Shanghai students, and pleads for the sake of the people in the Northeast who are in deep water and for the sake of the entire country that is in imminent danger. We swear to be loyal and foolish, dare to imitate the weeping in the Qin court, and will never leave Beijing until our goal is achieved. You have dedicated yourself to the country and made repeated declarations. At this time of national crisis, we respectfully ask you to follow the situation, approve our request, so as to show great faith and calm people's hearts. We are waiting for your orders with the utmost urgency. Respectfully presented to Chiang, Chairman of the National Government.

It is also reported that the students of the Municipal Wuben Girls' Middle School, since hearing of the fall of Heilongjiang Province, have become even more righteous. This time, the middle schools in the city organized a petition delegation to Beijing, and the school was also very enthusiastic. After the principal and teachers explained in succession yesterday, most of them understood the central government's policy of recovering lost territories. However, in order to take consistent action with the anti-Japanese work of various schools, they jointly elected more than 20 representatives to participate in the majority of the students, and they are still studying peacefully.

It was also reported that St. Mary's and McTyeire School for Girls would also send donations to the Anti-Japanese and National Salvation Association of the school for safekeeping. The Shanghai Bank sent someone to count the money, totaling 1,793 yuan, 7 jiao, and 8 fen, including 678 yuan, 2 jiao, and 6 fen from McTyeire School for Girls, and 545 yuan, 4 jiao, and 2 fen from St. Mary's. Those present at the scene to supervise were Zhao Xiuhong, a professor at the school, and Qiu Gaohua and Han Runpeng, representatives of the student union. It was also reported that Liu Zufa, chairman of the school's Anti-Japanese and National Salvation Association, had sent letters to the student union representatives of St. Mary's and McTyeire School for Girls, but they were unable to attend due to other matters. The middle school department is still conducting fundraising.

Free Talk

Recollections of Dai Liang 120

— Swallow

When the Sino-Japanese War broke out in 1894, I was only fifteen years old. I went to Ying County for the winter examination with my brothers Jingmeng and Lanzhou. The magistrate Wang Jiufang, whose name was Jinshi, was also a Jinshi. The first question of the first session was about strengthening the army, and the second question was about using war as a metaphor. The entire field had impassioned and generous words. I used Xue Rengui and Qi Cai Guang. My teacher, Gu Tiesheng, criticized it as inappropriate. In fact, it was caused by momentary anger. The inn always had the News, which was needed to relieve boredom after the health class. The alarming telegrams were transmitted remotely, and many were untrue. Most of them concealed defeats and reported victories. Every time I read them, I danced with joy. The final sentence of my poem, "Tell the chiefs of Hezhou, the king's army will sweep away the atmosphere soon," was quite appreciated by my classmates. My friend, Mr. Hu Qianliu, returned from Dongying and described that when they sent troops, the government and the people were worried about Army General Oshima Keisuke and Navy General Tojo, who were respected by the Japanese. They went to the front line and were lucky enough to win the first battle. The whole country celebrated, as if they were possessed. When the front line suffered a defeat at Ike Tang'a and another defeat at Song Qing, the alarming news came. Women and children wept. Those who went to various temples to pray were endless. When Wu Dazheng's entire camp was defeated, they laughed through tears again. They all said that they had been helped by the gods. Their superstitious behavior was laughable. However, their patriotism was more important than ours.

Fate of Wei Zhi 121

I heard that the Japanese attacked Ma Zhanshan, but the Japanese army did not enter Shanhaiguan. There is still a gate inside Shanhaiguan, and it is better to be inside the gate than outside. I heard that the Japanese army will enter the gate. The Japanese army did not climb Zijin Mountain. There is a river full of water under Zijin Mountain; the boatman watches with his hands in his sleeves as the boat capsizes?

Record of Praising Words on Li Shaoquan's Diplomacy 122

— Jianfu

Li Wenzhong, Duke of Hefei, during the Tongzhi and Guangxu reigns, his meritorious achievements shone brightly both domestically and internationally. Commentators have voiced reservations about his loyalty to the Qing Dynasty. However, his diplomatic talent is certainly commendable. Liang Zhuoru of Xinhui praised Li as a great man of his era, and this was not an overstatement. Now, with the Japanese invaders encroaching internally and the nation deteriorating daily, looking around the country, there is a genuine lack of diplomatic talent. Recalling Duke Li, one cannot help but feel a sense of yearning. Therefore, I have compiled several eulogies from famous Qing figures and recorded them for this discussion, hoping they will provide inspiration.

When the Central Plains is beset by troubles, with cunning bandits causing internal strife and powerful neighbors watching from abroad, it requires generals of extraordinary valor and statesmen with the responsibilities of both prime ministers and border officials to turn the tide and secure the realm. (Shen Bingcheng)

Since the opening of trade, disputes have frequently arisen. To clear the path through the Six Edicts, there was the Yantai Incident. To demand land along the Willow Palisade, there was the Xinjiang Incident. To seek refuge from the wind at Chihkan (Taiwan), there was the Langqiao Incident. To open customs at Vietnam, there was the Majiang Incident. With their insatiable demands and constant coercion, they would meet the dignitaries, lower their heads, and submit to appeasement. (Pan Shou)

Tianjin, located in a pivotal strategic area, serves as a crucial gateway to both oceans. When envoys from afar arrived, they observed the appearance and demeanor of the veteran statesman, and upon returning to their chiefs, they were filled with awe and dared not act presumptuously. (Hong Jun)

When he was transferred to govern Zhili, it was at a time when Western trade was beginning, and over fifty countries were establishing trade agreements. The imperial court appointed him as the Minister of Beiyang, stationed in Tianjin, to oversee all foreign affairs. He also concurrently managed coastal defense. Whether it was the arrival of foreign envoys, the travels of foreign merchants, or diplomatic disputes, he would assert authority and nip problems in the bud. What was particularly crucial to the nation's military and economic strategies was his pursuit of ways to enrich the country, without adhering to old conventions. Regarding the creation of ships, vehicles, weaponry, and the work of artisans, the ingenuity of machines, whatever the enemy was capable of, we could also do; whatever the enemy benefited from, we could also benefit from. (Tan Jixun)

At that time, the Western nations entering our ports lined up their sailing ships, each carrying their wealth and armaments, watching our borders intently. Duke Li connected with them through good faith and righteousness while strengthening our defenses internally. He stated that after more than ten years of war, both the public and private sectors were exhausted and that it was necessary to deeply cultivate our vitality. The Western nations were also awed by his prestige, and for a long time, none dared to treat us without due respect. Only the Russians broke their treaty in the Northeast, and the French stirred up trouble in the Southwest, but both soon returned to peaceful relations. Tang Dynasty history praised virtuous ministers, saying that Yao Chong was good at responding to changes, and Song Jing was good at upholding tradition. Duke Li possessed both qualities. (Xu Zhenyi)

Since the Tongzhi era, conflicts with foreign countries have included the Japanese invasion of Taiwan, the Russian demarcation of territory, and the French invasion of Vietnam, all of which involved deploying troops and engaging in combat. However, in some cases, land was surrendered, while in others, progress was slightly impeded before stopping. Finally, in the Vietnam War, despite the exchange of arrows, peace was ultimately restored through the presentation of silk and jade after the victory at Lang Son. During these critical moments, there was a sense that invasion was imminent. Duke Li, however, managed the secret matters, adapting to the changing circumstances, ultimately quelling the disturbances. Tianjin, as a critical location, was protected and enemy warships dared not enter or spy, unlike the past when they were able to bully and coerce us uncontrollably. Those who are thoughtful will understand the reason for this. (Liu Ruifen)

Once the maritime ban was lifted, dozens of countries eagerly sought to negotiate treaties with us. The coastal regions all looked to Beiyang as the starting point. Duke Li responded calmly and decisively, managing the situation with great trust and pacifying it with both gentleness and force. He prevented problems from arising and cultivated resources. He prepared for war, fortified defenses, and thoroughly implemented measures to uphold national dignity and handle diplomatic relations with care. (Zhang Xu)

Throughout history, the nature of arrogant rulers has been to fear power rather than appreciate virtue. The key to strategic planning lies in preparation and prevention. In the past, the western invaders obstructed our paths, and the eastern aggressors stirred up waves. Duke Li promoted Zou Yan's theories and formulated plans for transformation. He cultivated distant allies and warned those beyond the seas. His intellectual creativity was coupled with military strength, and he organized everything meticulously to encompass all aspects. All of the major measures taken in foreign affairs and coastal defense were sufficient to assist in ensuring the boundless peace of our nation. (Zhang Zhidong)

A Letter from Someone Who Moved from Jilin to Harbin 123

— Zhang Qilin

My close friend, Tao Jun, was in Jilin when the dwarf invaders occupied it. He has now moved to Harbin to escape their disturbance. I received a letter from him yesterday recounting his personal experiences and what he witnessed. Reading it makes one's hair stand on end in anger. I am sharing it in the newspapers to expose the crimes of the Japanese invaders. Readers, please do not underestimate this. Excerpts from the letter are as follows:

September 21st was the first day that the Japanese army occupied our Jilin. The people could do nothing. The Japanese army arrived in Jilin in the evening. Around 2:30 AM, our family was already asleep when we suddenly heard two gunshots in the alley. My brother woke up startled from his dream. Then, we heard a rapid, loud banging on the door, as if not done by hand. Knowing something was wrong, I quickly put on my clothes and went to peek outside. The small door had already been broken. Knowing we couldn't hold out for long, I called the servant to open the door. As soon as the door opened, two Japanese police officers stumbled in, each holding a long gun. One was still holding an iron hammer, likely used to break the door. After them, a man in Western clothing entered, speaking in Chinese, "Does Section Chief Wang of the Military Law Office live here?" (Mr. Wang did live in the lower house of my courtyard, but he moved away a few days ago.) He spoke in a very harsh tone. At that moment, one police officer shouted to his comrades, and another pointed his gun at my chest, placing the iron hammer on my forehead. At that moment, I had no choice but to say, "Mr. Wang did live here before, but he moved away some time ago." To my surprise, he angrily said, "Where did he go? You must know!" I replied that I didn't know. He became very angry, threatening to hit me. Just then, four Japanese soldiers rushed in, their bayonets gleaming. Two stood by the door, and two pressed their bayonets against my waist. At this moment, I was so frightened that I forgot about life and death and argued with them. I said, "He moved away because he didn't get along with my family. How would I know where he went?" They still didn't believe me and wanted me to lead them to find him. Seeing how things were, even if I told them, it would only hurt others. So I insisted on what I said. They repeatedly made motions to strike me with the iron hammer. Seeing that I would not change my story, they asked, "Do you have any Koreans in your house?" I replied no. Then they threatened me with their knives and guns. Fortunately, I was not swayed in the end. Then, they searched the house. At this time, my parents were hiding in the dark. One police officer broke into the room and shouted, "Got him!" and grabbed my father's hands, pulling him out. The man in Western clothing took out a photograph, which was my father's picture. The person in the photo was Mr. Wang. Luckily, Mr. Wang was tall and thin, while my father was short and stout. When they saw that they looked nothing alike, they released him and continued to search the other rooms. Finding nothing, they returned and asked my father's name. Then I showed them my business card. Seeing that I was not involved in the Liaoning military, they softened their tone slightly, and the sharp weapon in front of my chest was moved a little further away. They again asked my father where Mr. Wang was. My father said the same thing as I did. Seeing that there was no way to take advantage of the situation, they left angrily. Alas, our people live within our own territory, yet they are subjected to late-night searches and arrests by foreigners. What greater humiliation is there? What happened after that was even worse. It is unspeakable and makes one's hair stand on end in anger. One day, the Japanese army outside the East Gate also used the pretext of searching to force residents and merchants to kneel in the middle of the street. They went inside, overturning chests and cabinets. Small valuables and ornaments that could be put into bags were all taken away. Occasionally, young women and daughters were subjected to unavoidable rape. The schools were searched once, twice, three times. Ideologies were all thrown aside. If students were asked questions and were slow to answer, they were beaten. Some classmates who lived outside the city arrived at the city gate a little earlier and were made to kneel by the roadside until the sun was high before they could get up. During this time, there was no need to have classes in schools. But they were forced to do so. I can't bear to say more. In short, the whole situation is like a country that has been lost. My family does not want to be slaves of a conquered nation, so on October 17th, we fled to Harbin. I didn't dare to write a single word about the above matters in the letters when in Jilin because all mail had to be inspected. (Que Chou)

— Haike

In a certain place in Czechoslovakia, two maids were elected as members of the city council and participated in municipal affairs.

Fashionable women in England have recently started making boots and shoes from frog skin, adorned with peacock feathers.

A type of miniature pistol is currently popular throughout Europe, about the size of a fountain pen, filled with tear gas for self-defense when encountering thieves.

An American barber has invented a new hair pomade that emits a platinum-like glow when applied to the hair at night and can be washed off the next day.

Students at Oxford University in England must park their cars or motorcycles in the workshops designated by the university authorities to limit their outings to between 1:00 PM and 9:00 PM.

Clothing prices in New York are very expensive. Medium-quality fabrics that cost only four pounds in London cost twice as much in New York. The price of boots and shoes is also twice that of British goods, but they are not as durable.

— Jingheng

11) June 4th: The Japanese authorities plotted to assassinate Zhang Zuolin on the Beining Railway. 12) On June 7th, Japanese troops bombarded civilians and soldiers and looted over a thousand national defense firearms in Jiucun, Anqiu, Shandong. (12) On July 1st, Japanese soldiers illegally built roads in Hankou. (13) On July 26th, Japanese soldiers in Yingkou illegally practiced firing cannons and machine guns. (14) On September 23rd, Japanese residents in Shanghai privately trafficked arms. (15) In November, Japanese merchants in Shanghai privately transported over 2,200 kilograms of heroin. (16) On November 9th, a Japanese ship sank our Xinfeng Sea Liner. (17) Japanese merchants in Shanghai privately transported over 3,500 kilograms of heroin for the second time. At the same time, Japanese residents in Shanghai privately traded over a million yuan worth of opium. (18) On December 3rd, a Japanese ship in Wuhu viciously beat Mr. Chen, a Chinese citizen.

A Country Bumpkin Visits Shanghai Again (27) 126

— Bao Tianxiao

Actually, "cha shao" (叉燒) is a type of roasted pork. People from Guangdong love to eat it the most. Even in grand wedding ceremonies, this roasted pig is used as an important ritual, and a woman's virginity is also represented by this roasted pig. Because the roasted pig is roasted on iron skewers, it is simply called "cha shao." Unexpectedly, this country bumpkin confused "cha shao" with "chai shao" (拆梢), leading to a debate.

The country bumpkin thought: If I keep arguing with them, I don't know when I'll get to eat this meal. I'll just order a few dishes at random to fill my stomach. At that moment, he ordered a few dishes: braised pork with tofu, braised yellow croaker with salted vegetables, stir-fried shrimp with baiye (tofu skin), and stir-fried liver with chives. The waiter shook his head repeatedly and said in a series of quick replies:

(We don't have those dishes! We don't have those dishes!)

(Then the dishes you listed are all strange and bizarre. You want me to buy a gong, and then you talk about "chai shao" (拆梢), which is confusing. The dishes I ordered, you say you don't have, and you shake your head like a rattling drum. It seems like I'm going to come in with an empty stomach and leave with an empty stomach?) The country bumpkin became somewhat indignant and assertive.

(We are a Cantonese restaurant. The dishes we have are salt and pepper spare ribs, stir-fried shrimp with eggs, etc. Pick a few of those.)

The country bumpkin understood those dishes clearly, so he said:

(Alright! Just those dishes then.)

The Cantonese waiter thought, "Today, a country bumpkin has come." He chatted with another waiter in Cantonese, pointing at the country bumpkin, and unintentionally blurted out the phrase "diu na ma" (丟那媽).

(What are you saying?) the country bumpkin suddenly asked.

The Cantonese waiter thought that the country bumpkin wouldn't understand Cantonese, so he unintentionally blurted out a common curse word. Unexpectedly, the country bumpkin questioned him, as if he understood Cantonese. He quickly said:

(We didn't say anything. We were talking about our own things.) He quickly covered it up.

(It sounds like you were saying I came here to find a wet nurse. That's not the case. Although my nephew's wife, A Tu's new bride, gave birth to a little one, and they said she wanted to come to Shanghai to be a wet nurse for a wealthy family, we didn't encourage her to come. Those wealthy families who hire wet nurses only care about their own comfort and don't care about the lives of others. They lock the wet nurses in their houses, as if they were in prison. They aren't allowed to see their own husbands or even glance at their own children. Some, because they are greedy for a few coins, let their own children go hungry to death. It's truly pitiful. I don't encourage country people who can find a meal to come to the city to be wet nurses. Why are you saying that I came to Shanghai to find a wet nurse?)

Finance: Gold Market Shows Subtle Signs of Weakness 127

Fluctuations remain erratic. Yesterday's gold prices showed a slight decline. Although the volatility was not drastic, the overall price range was considerable, fluctuating by several taels each time. From morning to evening, there were about thirteen or fourteen taels of fluctuations. Traders felt uncertain, and there were significant discrepancies in buying and selling activities, ultimately resulting in a drop of more than six taels. The initial opening was weak, likely due to a slight drop in major trading. Subsequently, fluctuations became irregular, revolving around seventy taels. Exchange rates strengthened but then loosened, with some traders settling positions. British exchange rates hardened due to persistently small British-American exchange rates. The afternoon market saw high and low prices, with six to seven taels of fluctuation. Large holders sold off positions, and there was a slight upward trend at the close, with a total volume of over six hundred and seventy taels. Major traders may anticipate a rebound.

Morning hovered around seventy taels. The morning opened with a decline of three taels, to six hundred seventy-four taels and five qian. Major trading showed a recent decline of three-sixteenths, with no change in forward prices. Silver prices fell by seven-eighths, and private telegraphic transfers decreased by one fen, but this had no impact, likely due to selling by Shunli, Wanxing, and others. Buyers seemed strong for a moment, rising to seventy-seven taels, then declining by more than seven taels to sixty-nine taels and seven qian due to selling by Dadecheng, Yuanmao, Yonghengchang, Yong, and Mr. Wu. However, exchange rates, such as for US dollars, tightened. Mackellar offered 32.125 yuan, and HSBC absorbed February British gold at 19.1875. Hengchangyong, Tianfengyong, Yuanmaoyong, and others then entered, raising the price by seven taels in just over ten minutes. The published price of British gold did not change, and US dollars were quoted at a small seven-five, at seventy-six taels and nine qian. Suddenly, Hengxing, Bingxing, Shunli, and others all sold, and China Bank once bought and sold one-month British gold at twenty-five and offered US dollars at 32.3125. At 9:30, it dropped to seventy-one and a half taels. Exchange rates seemed to show interest, with forward US dollars at 32.1875 yuan, and with Tongtaichang, Yifengyong, Richang, Senchangyong, Qianchangxiang, and others competing to purchase, the price gradually rose by more than seven taels. At 10:00, the price was seventy-nine taels, and with Dalian dealers and Chengfengyong, Yuankangxiang, Senchangyong, Hengchangyong, Bingxing, and others selling in unison, the price could not hold for long and worsened, falling nearly ten taels, with only one or two taels of fluctuation. At 10:30, the price was sixty-nine and a half taels, and then it rose again by four taels, to seventy-three taels and seven or eight qian. But selling pressure arose again, with Tongtaichang, Yuanmaoyong, Dalian dealers, Yuanmao, Hengchangyong, and others selling in succession. US dollars could be settled at 32.275 to half a yuan, causing another drop of seven taels, to sixty-seven taels at 11:30. Subsequently, there were minor fluctuations of two to three taels. Bombay decreased by three annas, and at 11:45, it rose again by three taels, to seventy taels and eight qian at noon. Unexpectedly, the market closed at sixty-eight taels and nine qian, with scattered short covering pushing the price back above seventy taels. The quoted price was changed to seven hundred sixty-two taels, calculated with a deduction of seventy-five, seventy-six, up to ninety taels.

Afternoon market moved from high to low. The afternoon market opened at seventy-one and a half taels, then two and a half taels, reflecting the lingering effects of the noon closing. Suddenly, due to Bombay reporting a large five annas, the price retreated to sixty-eight taels. Before long, Wanxing, Dadecheng, Shunli, and others entered, and Mackellar absorbed one-month British gold at 4375, and Zhengjin and HSBC traded US dollars at 32.625 yuan, causing a rise of six taels, with only one or two taels of fluctuation. At 2:30, the price was seventy-three taels and nine qian. Subsequently, banks traded at 32.75 yuan and British gold at nine and a half pence. Hengxing, Fuchang, Yifengyong, Hengchangyong, Zhifengyong, and Yuanmaoyong all sold, resulting in a drop of more than eight taels. Market conditions became weak, and at 3:30, the price suddenly fell to sixty-five taels and five qian. Afterwards, conditions turned calmer, with various firms entering and short sellers covering positions. Exchange rates held steady, and sentiment shifted from weak to firm, with only one or two taels of fluctuation in half an hour. At 3:50, the price rose sharply, increasing by more than four taels. At 4:20, the price was seventy-one taels and four qian, and at the 4:30 closing, the price was seventy taels and eight qian, down six taels and seven qian compared to the previous day. Securities: Bond Prices Continue to Fall 131

Continued decline of about two to three yuan compared to previous levels

Market Closed for Three Days Starting Today for Settlement

The Shanghai Securities Exchange's November futures settlement period has arrived. Trading will be suspended from today onwards to facilitate various procedures before settlement. Today, initial account clearing will take place, with formal settlement scheduled for this Friday. This month's settlement volume is less than the approximately 20 million in October, so accounting will not be as heavy as before. Regarding yesterday's bond market conditions, spot transactions remained scarce, while futures prices continued to decline sharply, although trading was not entirely quiet. This was mainly due to the imminent settlement, leading to more transaction closures. However, compared to the previous day, the situation has slightly improved. Given the trend of bond prices, and the increasing influence of the Japanese, coupled with a tense diplomatic situation, the market is generally pessimistic. If there is no turnaround in the future, Sino-Japanese relations may inevitably break down, causing widespread anxiety and fragility in the market. Furthermore, news of new bond issuances further weakens the market. Although major players are not selling off significantly, small-scale sales are quite active. However, buyer sentiment remains extremely cold, with investors adopting a wait-and-see approach, leading to a significant imbalance between supply and demand. Consequently, prices continued to fall sharply, with several bonds nearing trading halts during the morning session. The situation continued to weaken at the start of the afternoon session, before slightly stabilizing by the close. As a result, compared to the previous day, except for the 1926 bonds, which remained stable, all other bonds fell by about two to three yuan, with the Reorganization bonds for November falling by a significant four yuan and three jiao. The bond market remains pessimistic. However, if the overall situation turns around, improvement is not impossible. Total spot transactions for the day amounted to 6,000 yuan, with futures transactions totaling over 8.1 million in the morning and over 4.4 million in the afternoon, adding up to 12.51 million yuan.

Yesterday's foreign rice market saw active spot sales on Ben Jie Street, while other merchants had no inquiries. Wheat Market Turns from Flat to Firm 138

Yesterday's wheat futures market generally showed a pattern of initial flatness followed by firmness. Initially, the decrease in overseas wheat quotations by 0.06-0.07 yuan caused uncertainty.
